According to the law, the definition of a full-time position is either full-time employment as is customary at the employee's workplace or she is employed in a position that encompasses at least 174 hours per month. Therefore, if the employee is employed in a position of less than 174 hours per month, the position is not considered full-time under the law. In addition, if the workplace has more hours of work per month as full-time, and the employee works fewer hours, her position is not considered full-time. Therefore, if the employee works only 6 or 7 hours a day due to the need to leave early to care for the children, thereby working less than 174 hours per month or less than what is customary as full-time at her workplace, her position is not considered full-time under the law.

 According to Section 13 of the Annual Leave Law, if an employee ceases to work before being granted the leave he was entitled to, the employer must pay him leave compensation in an amount equal to the leave pay that would have been payable to the employee if he had gone on leave on the day he ceased to work. According to the excerpts provided, during a time of emergency there are special provisions regarding employee rights and labor relations. There are provisions prohibiting the dismissal of employees during an emergency, as well as provisions stipulating that an employee's absence from work during an emergency will not be considered a termination of employment or affect his seniority. Also, the special provisions during an emergency are intended to add to employees' rights and not detract from them. They override provisions in employment contracts, collective agreements, and ordinary law. In addition, there is an increased duty of loyalty of the parties towards each other during an emergency.

According to the law, an employee serving in the reserves has special protections against dismissal. In addition, the reserve period is considered a period of work for the purpose of calculating seniority and accruing rights at the workplace. The law prohibits an employer from dismissing an employee due to his reserve service, and establishes a protection period of 30 days after the end of the service during which the employee may not be dismissed without special permission. In addition, the employee is entitled to continue to accrue seniority and rights at his workplace during the reserve period, as if he had continued to work normally. To the extent that there is no restriction, the employee is obliged to appear for his regular job even during the reserve period. If the employee works and serves in the reserves at the same time during hours outside of working hours, he will be entitled to reserve compensation in addition to his regular salary.

According to the extension order for reserve service members, wives/spouses of reservists are entitled to paid days of absence in addition to the existing law. The number of paid days of absence to which they are entitled will be in accordance with the number of cumulative reserve days. Thus, additional days of absence for 31 to 60 reserve days will be 2 days, 61 to 90 will be 4 days, 91 to 120 will be 6 days, and 121 days or more will be 8 days.

 According to the law, reserve service is not defined as work for someone who is not employed. However, someone who is not employed and serves in the reserves is entitled to receive compensation from the National Insurance Institute for reserve service.
 According to the law, a complaint about wage withholding can be filed with the Labor Court. The complaint can be filed by the employee himself or by the employee organization representing that workplace.
According to the Demobilized Soldiers Law, the employer must accept the employee back into the same position he held before the reserve, or into a similar position, under conditions that are not worse. If there is difficulty returning to work, it is worth contacting the employer and asking for assistance, for example, with retraining or temporary relief. According to Section 9(c)(1a) of the Women's Employment Law, an employee cannot be fired while on maternity leave or during a period of 60 days after the end of maternity leave, except with a special permit from the Minister of Industry, Trade and Employment. Therefore, while you are on maternity leave, you cannot be fired without receiving the aforementioned permit.
 According to the law, an employer is not obligated to pay wages to an employee who has been placed on unpaid leave. In your case, because you are being evacuated from the Enrichment Path and are defined as a red settlement, the employer is allowed to place you on unpaid leave and is not obligated to pay you wages. It is recommended that you check your eligibility for unemployment benefits with the National Insurance Institute.
 According to the law, if you have been laid off from your main job after a year and a half, and you are still working part-time at another job, your eligibility for unemployment benefits depends on the number of hours you work at the other job. If you work less than 20 hours a week on average, you are entitled to partial unemployment benefits based on the number of hours you work. If you work 20 hours a week or more on average, you are not entitled to unemployment benefits. To find out for sure your eligibility, it is recommended to contact the Employment Office and present them with your employment details.
 According to the law, the employer is obligated to pay wages to the employee even in the event of the closure of the business due to the state of emergency, as long as the employment relationship between the employer and the employee has not been terminated. The employer can submit a request for reimbursement of wage expenses from the state in accordance with the conditions set out in the outline. The law does not specifically refer to residents of red settlements, so the general guidelines also apply to them.
According to the law, it is not possible to cancel an Order 8 that has already been issued. The soldier is obligated to report for reserve service. However, in certain cases, it is possible to request a postponement or shortening of the service, if there is justification for this (for example, a health condition, a family event, etc.). To request this, one must contact the military unit that issued the order. If there are restrictions on performing work concurrently with reserve service, one must notify the employer in advance.
 According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee who has received Order 8 during service and for 30 days after its termination, except with special approval from the Employment Committee. The firings will be void if made without such approval.
According to the law, an employer is not obligated to pay for vacation days that are not actually used by the employee due to reserve service. However, if there is a collective agreement or other arrangement between the employer and the employees that states that vacation days that are not actually used due to reserve service must be paid for, then that agreement must be followed. In the absence of such an agreement, the employer is not obligated by law to pay for vacation days that are not actually used due to reserve service.

 According to the law, a normal workday may not exceed 8 hours. For night work and on the eve of a holiday or Shabbat, the workday may not exceed 7 hours.

According to the law, the number of days of annual leave that an employee is entitled to depends on the number of years of seniority with that employer: - For each of the first 5 years - 16 days of leave - For the sixth year - 18 days of leave - For the seventh year - 21 days of leave - From the eighth year onwards - an additional day of leave for each year, up to a maximum of 28 days of leave. Also, if the employee worked less than 200 days a year for that employer, the number of days of leave he is entitled to will be calculated in proportion to the number of days he actually worked. If there is no information about the employee's seniority or the number of days he worked, it is not possible to calculate exactly how many days of leave he is entitled to.
According to the law, the employer can receive a refund from the state for the payment of wages to employees who were not placed on unpaid leave, without a time limit. However, there may be administrative guidelines that limit the length of time during which the employer can receive a refund, but this is not enshrined in the law. In addition, the law does not refer to the employee's age as a factor affecting the employer's eligibility for a refund.

According to the law, after giving birth, a woman is entitled to a maternity and parenting period of 26 weeks, of which 7 weeks or less before the birth, at the woman's choice, and the remainder after the birth. In addition, the law allows for extensions of the maternity and parenting period in certain cases, such as the birth of more than one child or hospitalization of the mother or newborn.

In the event of a violation of rights, employees have the right to sue in the Labor Court or through the workers' organization.

According to the extension order for reserve service members, spouses of reservists are entitled to paid days of absence in addition to the existing law. The number of paid days of absence to which they are entitled will be in accordance with the number of cumulative reserve days of the spouses. Thus, the additional days of absence for 31 to 60 reserve days will be 2 days, 61 to 90 will be 4 days, 91 to 120 will be 6 days, and 121 days or more will be 8 days.

According to the law, a pregnant employee cannot be fired simply because she is a "bad and ugly employee." In order to fire a pregnant employee who has worked for at least 6 months, a special permit is required from the Commissioner for Women's Employment Law at the Ministry of Labor.
According to the law, an employer is prohibited from dismissing a pregnant employee without obtaining a special permit from the Commissioner of the Women's Employment Law at the Ministry of Labor, if she has worked for him for at least 6 months. In addition, the law prohibits dismissing an employee who is a single mother of children under the age of 14 living with her, due to absence from work due to the closure of educational institutions due to the state of emergency, if it is not possible to look after the children. Therefore, you cannot be dismissed based on the description you provided, without holding a hearing and obtaining all the necessary permits. If you were unlawfully dismissed, the dismissal is void.  According to the law, an hourly employee serving in the reserves is entitled to receive his regular salary for the hours of work he missed due to service, in addition to compensation from the National Insurance Institute for the period of reserve service.  According to the law, there are restrictions on firing employees on reserve duty: 1. It is prohibited to fire an employee who has been on reserve duty for more than 60 days, during the reserve period and for the 60 days following it, except with the approval of a supervisory committee. 2. It is prohibited to fire an employee who has served in the reserves for more than two consecutive days but less than 60 days, for the 30 days following the end of the reserve, without obtaining a permit. 3. Firing an employee due to reserve duty, call-up to the reserves or anticipation of reserve duty - are null and void. 4. Absence from work due to reserve duty is not considered a break in the continuity of work in the factory.

According to the law, there is an obligation to return an employee to work after reserve service, even if the employee began working at the workplace only after the period of reserve service. Section 6 of the Discharged Soldiers Law states that a discharged soldier who was a permanent employee at a factory shortly before his enlistment must be accepted back to the job he worked at before enlistment, or to a similar job, under no less favorable conditions. The obligation applies whether the employee began working before enlistment or after. Therefore, the answer to your question is that there is an obligation to return an employee to work even if he began working after the period of reserve service.

Hello Eran, according to the law, if you have performed at least 60 days of reserve service starting from October 7, 2023, the employer is prohibited from firing you for 60 days from the end of the reserve period. Therefore, in the first case that you mentioned that you performed 65 days of reserve service, the employer is prohibited from firing you for 60 days from the end of the last reserve period. In the second case that you performed 93 days of reserve service and in the third case that you performed 123 days of reserve service, the prohibition on the employer from firing you is the same prohibition - 60 days from the end of the last reserve period. According to the law, a reserve soldier has several main rights:1. Prohibition of dismissal - It is prohibited to dismiss a reserve soldier due to his reserve service.2. Continued accumulation of seniority and rights at work - During the period of reserve service, the soldier continues to accumulate seniority and rights at his place of work.3. Payment of wages - During the period of reserve service, the soldier is entitled to payment of wages from the employer and compensation from the National Insurance Institute.4. 30 days of protection - The prohibition of dismissal also applies 30 days after the end of reserve service.5. Dismissal permit - A reserve soldier can only be dismissed with a permit from the Employment Committee.

According to the law, during a time of emergency, it is prohibited to fire employees in the following cases: 1. It is prohibited to fire an employee for being absent from work or for failing to perform work due to instructions given during an attack or in a special situation on the home front. 2. It is prohibited to fire an employee who is absent from work to care for his child due to the closure of an educational institution during an emergency, under certain conditions (for example, if the child is in his sole custody or the spouse cannot care for the child). 3. It is prohibited to fire an employee who is absent to care for his child due to the military service of the spouse or other parent. 4. With regard to contractor employees, termination of employment (even temporarily) is prohibited under similar circumstances. 5. It is prohibited to fire an employee who has been drafted for work service during an emergency without special permission. In all these cases, dismissals in violation of the provisions of the law will be void.

According to the law, an employee has a number of basic rights: 1. Right to maintain existing rights: The law states that its provisions do not derogate from any right granted to an employee by law, collective agreement, employment contract or custom. 2. Right to request remote work: The employee may request to work from home, and the employer is obliged to consider the request in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner, taking into account the existing circumstances. 3. Right to consent regarding unpaid leave: Taking unpaid leave (unpaid leave) requires the consent of both the employer and the employee. 4. Right to unemployment benefits under certain conditions: In the event of taking unpaid leave at the initiative of the employer, the employee may be entitled to unemployment benefits if he meets the eligibility conditions. It is important to note that these rights are subject to specific conditions and circumstances, and each case must be examined on its own merits.
 According to the Sick Pay (Absence Due to Child Illness) Law, 5753-1993, a parent of children under the age of 5 has the following rights: 1. A parent is entitled to credit up to 8 days of absence per year due to their child's illness, against their accumulated sick days, if their spouse works and is not absent from work for this purpose. 2. If the child is in the sole custody of the parent, or the parent is an independent parent, they are entitled to credit up to 16 days of absence per year due to their child's illness. 3. These rights apply to children up to the age of 16, including children under the age of 5. It is important to note that this law is intended to add to the employee's rights by law or agreement and not to detract from them.

According to the law, after being released from one month of reserve service, you have a number of rights: 1. Maintaining seniority: The period in which you served in the reserves is considered a period of work at the factory for the purpose of calculating seniority. This includes rights dependent on seniority such as vacation days, sick days, and severance pay. 2. Protection against being taken on unpaid leave: The employer is not permitted to take you on unpaid leave for 60 days after the end of reserve service without obtaining special permission. 3. Return to work: You have the right to return to your previous job, unless there is a justifiable reason for a change. It is important to note that unless otherwise stated, there is an obligation to report to work after being released from the reserves.
According to the law, "parental leave" (or "parenting time") is a right granted to working parents. Section 7B of the Women's Employment Law specifies the conditions for exercising the right to parenting time: 1. An employee may exercise the right to parenting time alone or alternately with his or her partner. 2. The spouse's consent is required for exercising the right alternately or by the spouse. 3. A signed declaration must be submitted to the employer at least 21 days before the end of the birth and parenting period. 4. The declaration must specify the days on which each spouse will exercise the parenting time. 5. The manner of exercising the right can be changed in agreement with the employer. It is important to note that the total quota of parenting hours for both spouses will not exceed what the employee would have been entitled to alone.
 No, it is prohibited to dismiss a pregnant employee who has worked for at least 6 months for the same employer or in the same workplace, except with special permission from the Minister of Labor and Social Affairs. The Minister will not authorize dismissals if they are pregnancy-related in his opinion. This prohibition applies to both permanent and temporary employees. It should be noted that "dismissal" also includes the non-renewal of a fixed-term employment contract under certain conditions.
According to the law, dismissals due to reserve service are illegal. According to the Annual Leave Law, 5711-1951:1. Every employee is entitled to annual leave in accordance with the provisions of the law.2. An employee is not permitted to work for pay during his vacation days. If he worked regular paid work during the vacation, he loses his right to vacation pay, and the employer is entitled to deduct the vacation pay paid to him from his salary.3. The employer is entitled to take the employee on annual leave of up to 7 days without prior notice. Regarding leave of more than 7 days, the employer must notify the employee of this two weeks in advance.4. Unused vacation days can be accumulated for the next two years, without the employer's approval, under certain conditions such as: failure to receive leave despite entitlement, absence due to reserve duty, or work in an essential enterprise.

According to the law, an employer may not harm an employee's income due to reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. No, you may not be fired during reserve service. According to the law, an employer is prohibited from firing an employee during his or her reserve service period. Furthermore, if your reserve service lasts for more than two consecutive days, the prohibition on firing also continues for 30 days after the end of reserve service. In the case of reserve service lasting more than 60 days, the period of protection from firing is extended to 60 days after the end of service. Any firing contrary to these provisions will be void.
Under Israeli law, employees cannot automatically request remote work. The decision regarding remote work is part of the employer’s administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee’s request to work from home in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the existing circumstances. In other words, employees can request to work remotely, but the final decision rests with the employer.

Therefore, while employees can request to work remotely, they do not have an absolute right to demand it, and this depends on the employer's discretion.

According to the Women's Labor Law, a pregnant woman cannot be fired without special permission. The law states that an employer may not fire an employee who is pregnant and has not yet entered the period of childbirth and parenthood, except with permission from the Minister of Labor and Social Affairs. The Minister will not authorize dismissals if, in his opinion, they are related to pregnancy. This provision applies to both permanent and temporary employees, provided that the employee has worked for the same employer or in the same workplace for at least six months.

No, the employer cannot fire you immediately after reserve service under Order 8 without special permission. According to the law, if your reserve service was more than two consecutive days, the employer may not fire you for 30 days after the end of reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. If your reserve service was more than 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of reserve service. In addition, the law states that dismissals due to reserve service, call-up to the reserves or anticipation of reserve service are void. If the employer wishes to fire you during this period, he must obtain special permission from the Employment Committee and prove that the dismissal is not related to your reserve service.
 According to the law, vacation days are not considered actual work days for the purpose of calculating annual leave entitlement. The law refers to the number of actual work days during the year for the purpose of determining vacation entitlement, and does not include the vacation days themselves in this calculation. For example, the law states that an employee who has worked at least 200 days in a year is entitled to the full number of vacation days, while an employee who has worked less than 200 days is entitled to a prorated portion of the vacation days. The vacation days themselves are not included in the 200 days.
According to the law, the employer must continue to pay pension contributions even during reserve service, including in Order 8. Section 36(a) of the Demobilized Soldiers Law states that the employer and the employee (or the employer alone, as the case may be) must continue to pay contributions to the pension fund during the period of military service, at the same rates that were used to pay before the employee enlisted. Therefore, the employer is prohibited from stopping pension payments during reserve service in Order 8.

According to the Hours of Work and Rest Law, 5711-1951, a full workweek is defined as no more than 45 hours of work. A normal workday may not exceed 8 hours of work, and on certain days such as Shabbat Eve or a holiday, the workday is limited to 7 hours.
 According to the Hours of Work and Rest Law, 5711-1951, a workday shall not exceed eight hours of work. However, in night work and on the day before the weekly rest day and on the day before a holiday on which the employee does not work, the workday shall not exceed seven hours of work.

The law does not specify an exact number of permitted overtime hours, but rather states that overtime employment is permitted only under certain conditions. For more details regarding the exact conditions for permitting overtime work, it is recommended to refer to Sections 10 and 11 of the law.

According to the Women's Labor Law, a pregnant employee is entitled to a number of protections: 1. She may be absent from work for medical examinations related to pregnancy, if the doctor has approved it in writing. This absence is considered an absence due to illness. 2. If the doctor has determined that the type of work, the place of work, or the manner in which it is performed endangers the employee or the fetus, she may be absent from work. This absence will be considered unpaid leave, but will not affect rights dependent on seniority. 3. An employer may not dismiss a pregnant employee who has worked for at least 6 months without special permission from the Commissioner of the Women's Labor Law at the Ministry of Labor. 4. A pregnant employee may not be placed on unpaid leave without her consent, if she has worked for at least 6 months for that employer.
 According to the law, a discharged soldier is defined as someone who was a soldier and was discharged from service. In the case of Order 8, you are considered a conscript called to report under the Defense Service Law. According to Section 22 of the Emergency Labor Service Law, a conscript called to report under the Defense Service Law is exempt from labor service obligations for the period of his reporting as well as for the period of his service following reporting. That is, while you are serving under Order 8, you are exempt from other labor service obligations.

Under Israeli law, termination of an employment contract can be considered a dismissal under certain circumstances. In the context of the Emergency Workers Protection Law, the law specifically refers to contractor employees and defines that a permanent or temporary cessation of the employment of a contractor employee will be considered a dismissal. The law states that “if the employer is a labor contractor, a permanent or temporary cessation of the employee’s employment will also be considered a dismissal for the purposes of this section.” However, it is important to note that the law does not explicitly address all types of employment contracts, and therefore the specific circumstances of each case may need to be considered.

 According to Israeli law, there is no specific reference to flexible working hours in the employment contract. According to the law, an employee whose spouse is on reserve duty is entitled to a reduction in the working day by one hour per day, under the following conditions: 1. The spouse's reserve duty period is at least 5 consecutive days. 2. The employee has a child under the age of 13 who is with him. 3. The employee is employed full-time. 4. It is important to note that this right does not apply on days when the employee is already absent from work due to other parental duties.

According to the Discharged Soldiers (Return to Work) Law, 1949, the employer is obligated to return an employee to his or her job after reserve service. Section 6(a) of the law states that the employer must accept the employee back to the job he or she worked in before enlistment, under conditions that are no worse than those prior to enlistment. If this is not practically possible, the employer must accept the employee in the best possible job and under the best possible conditions. If you are having difficulty returning to work for personal reasons, it is recommended that you talk to your employer and try to find a solution that will make your return easier, such as a gradual return or temporary adjustments to your job. It is important to remember that the law protects your right to return to work, but also requires you to report to work as required.

As a new employee, you have a number of basic rights under Israeli labor laws: 1. Right to annual leave: According to the Annual Leave Law, every employee is entitled to paid annual leave. 2. Rights under agreements: The law protects additional rights that you may have under a collective agreement, employment contract or workplace practice. 3. Weekly rest: You have the right to weekly rest, and if you are asked to work on rest days, you have the right to refuse. 4. Maintaining working conditions: The employer may change your working conditions, but only in a reasonable manner. 5. Right to a hearing: In the event of a material change in the terms of your employment or dismissal, you have the right to a hearing before a final decision is made. It is important to note that these are only some of the basic rights, and you may have additional rights depending on your specific terms of employment.

No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (Reserve Recruitment Order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired even for 30 days after the end of the reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. If the duration of reserve service exceeds 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the service. Dismissals in violation of these provisions will be void.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (Reserve Order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call-up to reserve service, or his expected service in reserve service. In the case of reserve service exceeding two consecutive days, it is prohibited to fire the employee or to harm the scope of his job or his income without special permission from the Employment Committee, even for 30 days after the end of reserve service. If dismissals were made in violation of this law, the dismissals are void.

If the employee has been working for less than six months, the protection against dismissal under Section 9(a) of the Women's Employment Law does not apply to her. That is, in this case the employer is not required to obtain special permission from the Commissioner of the Women's Employment Law at the Ministry of Labor to dismiss the pregnant employee.

According to the law, a man is entitled to maternity leave in several cases: 1. An employee may take 7 days of maternity leave during his wife's period of childbirth and parenthood, provided that she waives the last week of her maternity pay. 2. An employee may take part of his wife's period of childbirth and parenthood (partial maternity leave), starting from the seventh week after the birth, if his wife agrees to waive part of her period and return to work. 3. In special cases, such as when the mother is unable to care for the child due to disability or illness, the employee is entitled to take the remainder of the period of childbirth and parenthood in her place. 4. A single father or in the event that the child is in the father's sole custody, he is entitled to a full period of childbirth and parenthood. It should be noted that the exact length of the period depends on the specific circumstances and the consent of the spouse.

 No, as a general rule, it is prohibited to fire a pregnant employee. According to the Women's Employment Law, an employer may not fire an employee who is pregnant and has not yet entered the period of childbirth and parenthood, except with special permission from the Minister of Labor and Social Affairs. This prohibition applies to both permanent and temporary employees, provided that the employee has worked for the same employer or in the same workplace for at least six months. The Minister will not authorize dismissals if, in his opinion, they are related to pregnancy.

According to the law, in times of emergency, it is permissible to employ workers overtime. The Minister of Labor may permit this when a decision has been made to declare an emergency and the state of the economy requires it. Regarding payment for these hours, the law does not explicitly state the method of payment during an emergency. However, as a rule, working overtime entitles you to higher pay. It is recommended to check the collective agreements or personal employment contract regarding the exact payment terms during an emergency.
According to the law, an employee who worked with evacuees from war is protected from dismissal due to his absence from work or failure to perform work during the temporary order period. Section 2(b1)(1)(a) of the Emergency Workers Protection Law states that an employer shall not dismiss an employee who has evacuated from his place of residence which is located in a locality listed in the appendix to the law. In addition, the period of work with evacuees is considered a regular period of work for the purpose of the employee's rights.

According to the law, firefighters are considered employees of a rescue service. Section 11 of the Emergency Workers Protection Law states that the provisions of the chapter will not apply to an employee of a rescue service as defined in Section 90A of the Police Ordinance. This means that as a firefighter, you are required to report to work even in an emergency, and the protections against dismissal stipulated in this law for other employees do not apply to you.

According to the law, a manager is prohibited from asking an employee to do something illegal. Section 27(a) of the Working Hours and Rest Law states that members of management, managers and officials are personally liable for employment in violation of the law. The manager may be liable for the offense and be punished if he fails to prove that he took all appropriate measures to ensure compliance with the provisions of the law. Therefore, a manager may not ask an employee to perform illegal actions, as this may impose personal liability on him.

No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (Reserve Recruitment Order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired even for 30 days after the end of the reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. If the duration of reserve service exceeds 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the service. Dismissals in violation of these provisions will be void.

If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired during his service and for 30 days after the end of his reserve service, except with special permission from the Employment Committee. If the employee serves for more than 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the reserve service. In the event of a dismissal in violation of these provisions, the dismissal is void.
Under Israeli law, the decision to work remotely is part of the employer’s administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee’s request to work from home in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the prevailing circumstances. Therefore, while employees can request to work remotely, they do not have an absolute right to demand it, and this depends on the employer’s decision and the specific circumstances.

According to the law, if your manager insists that you do something illegal, there is no need to call the police (100). Instead, the law places responsibility on the members of the management and the managers themselves. Section 27 of the Working Hours and Rest Act states that members of the management, managers and officials may be liable for violations of the law, unless they can prove that the violation was committed without their knowledge or that they took all reasonable measures to prevent it. If you feel that your manager is asking you to do something illegal, it is recommended that you document the request and contact competent authorities within the company or the Ministry of Labor for advice and guidance.

 According to the Women's Employment Law, a pregnant employee who has worked for at least 6 months for the same employer or in the same workplace cannot be fired, except with a special permit from the Minister of Labor and Social Affairs. The Minister will not authorize dismissals if they are, in his opinion, related to pregnancy. To fire a pregnant employee, the employer must contact the Supervisor of the Women's Employment Law at the Ministry of Labor and request a special permit. Only after receiving the permit can the employee be fired.

According to the law, after reserve service in Order 8, protection against dismissal depends on the duration of reserve service: 1. If the reserve service was over 60 days (two months), the employer is prohibited from dismissing the employee for 60 days (two months) after the end of the reserve without special permission. 2. If the reserve service was over two consecutive days but less than 60 days, the employer is prohibited from dismissing the employee for 30 days (one month) after the end of the reserve without permission. It is important to note that in any case, it is prohibited to dismiss an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service or expected service in the reserves.

Example question: Is an employee who is the parent of a child with a disability entitled to be absent from work in order to care for his child? Answer: Yes, according to the Sick Pay (Absence Due to Child Illness) Law, an employee who is the parent of a person with a disability and has worked for at least a year for that employer is entitled to credit up to 18 days of absence per year against his sick days or vacation, for the purpose of providing personal assistance to his child. In addition, under certain conditions, the employee is entitled to an additional 18 days. In addition, the employee is entitled to be absent for up to 52 hours per year without deduction from his salary for the purpose of providing personal assistance to his child with a disability.

In particular, pay attention to payment for overtime and work on the weekly rest day:1. According to the law, the employer must continue to make payments to pension funds and similar funds even during the employee's period of military service, including weekends. Section 36(a) of the Discharged Soldiers (Return to Work) Law states that the employer and the soldier (or the employer alone, as the case may be) must make payments to the fund at the rates that were customary before the soldier's enlistment, and this for the entire period from the date of his enlistment until his return to work or until the day of his discharge. The law does not distinguish between weekdays and weekends, and therefore the obligation applies to the entire period, including weekends.

By law, the employer and the employee (or the employer alone, as the case may be) must continue to make payments to pension funds, benefits, or similar funds during the employee's reserve service period. The payments must be at the same rates as those paid before the employee's enlistment in the reserves. If the employee did not pay his share of the payments during reserve service, he will be required to complete the payments after his release within a period of up to three times the length of his reserve service period. The employer may pay his share concurrently with the employee's payments. It is important to note that the payment obligation applies even if the employee has not returned to work after reserve service, until the day of his release from service.

This is in accordance with Section 10 of the Sick Pay Law, 1976. Under Israeli law, employees cannot automatically request remote work. The decision regarding remote work is part of the employer’s administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee’s request to work from home in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the existing circumstances. In other words, employees can request to work remotely, but the final decision rests with the employer.
According to the law, the employer can obtain a special permit to take a pregnant employee on unpaid leave (GLT) from the Commissioner of the Women's Employment Law at the Ministry of Labor. The employer must submit an application for a permit and prove that there are special circumstances justifying this, such as the closure of the business due to an emergency. It is important to note that without such a permit, the employer is prohibited from taking a pregnant employee who has worked for at least 6 months on unpaid leave without her consent.
Regarding Order 8 (Reserve Service in Emergency Circumstances), the law establishes special protections for employees: 1. An employer is prohibited from dismissing an employee who has a child, or from placing him on unpaid leave, during the period of reserve service of his spouse or the child's other parent, as well as for 14 days after the end of the service, except with a special permit. 2. This protection applies when the reserve service is in emergency circumstances according to Section 8 of the Reserve Service Law (Order 8), or when the actual or expected duration of service is at least 21 consecutive days. 3. The employee is required to notify the employer in writing of the reserve service of his spouse or other parent within 3 working days from the moment the employer announced its intention to dismiss or place him on unpaid leave. 4. The employee's absence from work during this period will not be considered a break in the continuity of his work and will not affect the rights dependent on seniority.

According to the law, an employer does not have the right to fine an employee as part of the employment relationship. The law defines penalties and fines only in the case of a violation of the law by the employer or interference with the actions of a labor inspector. The law does not address the possibility of an employer imposing fines on his employees. Therefore, as a general rule, it is not legal for an employer to fine his employees.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (reserve recruitment order) without a special permit. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. In the event of such dismissals, the dismissals will be void. In addition, there is protection against dismissal during and after reserve service: 1. For reserve service of more than two consecutive days and up to 60 days - the employee may not be fired during the service and 30 days after its completion without a permit. 2. For reserve service of more than 60 days - the employee may not be fired during the service and 60 days after its completion without a permit. In these cases, the employer must obtain a special permit from the Employment Committee to fire the employee, and the permit will only be granted for special reasons and if it is proven that the dismissal is not related to reserve service.

However, the employer must consider the employee's request to work remotely in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the existing circumstances. According to the law, an employee who served in the reserves for more than two consecutive days cannot be fired without permission from the Employment Committee for 30 days after the end of the reserve service. In the case of reserve service exceeding 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the service. Therefore, assuming that your service under Order 8 exceeded two consecutive days, your employer cannot summon you for a hearing immediately upon your return. He must wait at least 30 days after the end of the reserve service, and if you served more than 60 days, he must wait 60 days. It is important to note that a summons to a hearing made before the war is not necessarily void, but the employer is obliged to respect the period of protection stipulated by law after the end of the reserve service before continuing with the dismissal proceedings.

Yes, days off work continue to accrue during reserve service. According to the Discharged Soldiers (Return to Work) Law, an employee's absence from work due to reserve service will not be considered a break in the continuity of his work at the factory. In addition, the law states that for the purposes of rights dependent on seniority, the reserve period is considered a period of work at the factory. Therefore, the accumulation of vacation days continues as usual even during reserve service.

If you have been fired, there are several steps you can take:1. Check whether the dismissal was legal: The law prohibits dismissal in certain circumstances, such as during or after reserve service, or during a certain state of emergency.2. Make sure you were given a proper hearing: Every employee has the right to a hearing before being fired or having their employment conditions materially changed.3. If the dismissal was against the law (for example, without a hearing or during a protected period), the dismissal may be void.4. No, you may not be fired while you are in the reserves. According to the law, an employer is prohibited from firing an employee during his or her reserve service period. According to the law, compensation for reserve service is provided by the National Insurance Institute and not by the employer. Regarding employees with a monthly salary, there are cases in which employees receive compensation through the employer, without filing a personal claim. Under Israeli law, the decision to work remotely is part of the employer's administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee's request to work from home in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the prevailing circumstances. Therefore, while employees can request to work remotely, they do not have an absolute right to demand it, and this depends on the employer's discretion.
According to the Sick Pay Law, 1976, an employee who is absent from work due to illness is entitled to receive sick pay from his employer, subject to the maximum eligibility period. If you submitted a medical certificate and had sick days to use, the employer is obligated to pay you sick pay for the period during which you were sick in the last month of your employment. It is important to note that the law states that payment begins from the fourth day of absence (100% of the salary), and for the second and third days, 50% of the salary is paid. The first day is not paid, unless otherwise stipulated in the regulations. If the employer refuses to pay the sick pay even though you met the required conditions, you can contact the Labor Court or the Ministry of Labor and Social Affairs for assistance in this matter.

If you wish to receive more detailed information, it is recommended that you contact the National Insurance Institute directly or the entities that handle victims of hostilities.

According to the law, there is no specific reference to a request for remote work after long reserve service. However, the law states that the employer must return the employee to his job after reserve service, under conditions that are no worse than those before the service. Regarding remote work, the law states that it is conditional on the employer's consent. Therefore, remote work can be requested, but the employer is not obligated to agree to it. If there is no consent to remote work, there is an obligation to report to work as usual.
According to the Hours of Work and Rest Law, 5711-1951, employing an employee overtime is prohibited, unless it is permitted under Section 10 or permitted under Section 11 of the law. The law states that a work week shall not exceed 45 working hours. Therefore, in general, it is not possible to work more than 12 hours on a regular workday, unless there are special permits or emergency situations that allow this.

 According to the Sick Pay Law, the value of a sick day is calculated as follows: 1. For a salaried employee - the sick pay will be the amount of the wage the employee would have been entitled to receive if he had continued working. 2. For an employee whose salary is paid according to the quantity of produce - the sick pay will be the amount of the wage the employee would have been entitled to receive if he had continued working and produced the average quantity of produce per working day that he produced in the three months preceding his illness. It is important to note that in the first days of the illness, payment may be partial or not given at all, in accordance with the law.
According to the law, for a salaried employee, the period of illness includes all days of illness, including weekly rest days and holidays. Therefore, in your case, the first day of illness will be counted from Friday, which is the first day you are absent from work due to illness. This is despite the fact that Friday and Saturday are weekly rest days. It is important to note that according to the law, payment of sick pay begins on the fourth day of absence, with half of the sick pay being paid for the second and third days, and the first day not being paid at all.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in reserve service. In the event of a dismissal in violation of this law, the dismissal is null and void. In addition, an employee may not be fired during his reserve service period, as well as for a certain period after the end of his service (30 days or 60 days, depending on the length of reserve service), except with special permission from the Employment Committee. Such a permit will be granted only for special reasons and if it is proven that the dismissal is not related to reserve service.

According to the law, an employer is not permitted to fire an employee for being absent from work to care for his child, who is with him, due to the closure of the educational institution where the child is studying or staying due to an order given during an attack or during a special situation on the home front. This is provided that one of the following has been met: the child is in the sole custody of the employee, the employee is an independent parent, or the employee's spouse is not absent from work to care for the child. Also, this provision will not apply if the employee's or his spouse's workplace had adequate arrangements for caring for the child. Therefore, if the educational settings were closed by order of the Home Front Command, and you are absent from work to care for your child under these conditions, the law protects you from dismissal due to this absence.

The duty to hear is given to every employee before his dismissal or before a substantial change in his employment conditions. It means that the employer must allow the employee to express his views before making a final decision on his case.

According to the information provided, there is a possibility of financial assistance for those who live on the conflict line and did not receive a salary at the beginning of the war. The law refers to employees who were absent from work between 07.10.2023 and 30.6.2024 due to the security situation. If you live in an evacuated locality and are absent from work due to the security situation, you may be entitled to a payment. The amount of the payment will be your regular salary, without supplements, up to a ceiling of 1,510 NIS per day. It is important to note that the payment is supposed to be paid by the employer on the salary payment date in the month following the date of publication of the extension order. The employer may be entitled to a refund from the Tax Authority for this payment. It is recommended to contact your employer and find out your exact eligibility according to your specific circumstances.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (Reserve Recruitment Order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired even for 30 days after the end of the reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. If the duration of reserve service exceeds 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the service. Dismissals in violation of these provisions will be void.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (reserve call-up order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call-up to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. In the event of such dismissals, the dismissals will be void. In addition, there is protection against dismissal during and after the reserve period: 1. For reserve service of more than two consecutive days and less than 60 days: The employee may not be fired during the service and for 30 days after its completion, without special permission. 2. For reserve service of 60 days or more: The employee may not be fired during the service and for 60 days after its completion, without special permission. It is important to note that absence due to reserve service is not considered a break in the employee's continuous work.

According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in reserve service. If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired during the reserve period and for 30 days after the end of the service, without permission from the Employment Committee. If the duration of service exceeds 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of the service. Dismissals made in violation of these provisions will be void.
No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (reserve call-up order) without special permission. The law prohibits firing an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call-up to reserve service, or his expected service in reserve service. In the event of a dismissal in violation of this law, the dismissal is void. In addition, there is protection against dismissal during and after the reserve period, depending on the length of service: - For reserve service of more than two consecutive days and up to 60 days: It is prohibited to fire during the service and for 30 days after it without permission. - For reserve service of more than 60 days: It is prohibited to fire during the service and for 60 days after it without permission. It is important to note that absence due to reserve service is not considered a break in continuous work.
 According to the law, the decision to work remotely is part of the employer's administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee's request to work remotely in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the existing circumstances. Therefore, while employees can request to work remotely, they do not have an absolute right to demand it, and this depends on the employer's discretion.
 No, justified absence due to an emergency does not count towards sick leave. According to the Emergency Workers Protection Law, an employee's absence from work in the circumstances of an emergency will not be considered a break in the continuity of his work and will not affect the rights dependent on the employee's seniority with his employer. In other words, such absence is not considered as using sick leave and does not affect the employee's rights.

 According to the extension order for reserve service members, spouses of reserve service members are entitled to paid days of absence based on the number of days the spouse has accumulated in reserve service. Payment for these days will be at the employee's regular salary, without supplements, up to a ceiling of NIS 1,510 per day. It is important to note that entitlement to paid days of absence only begins when the spouse has served 31 days or more in reserve service.

According to the Annual Leave Law, the length of annual leave depends on the number of years of work with the employer: - In the first five years: 16 days of leave per year - In the sixth year: 18 days of leave - In the seventh year: 21 days of leave - From the eighth year onwards: an additional day for each year of work, up to a maximum of 28 days of leave per year. It is important to note that this entitlement is full for employees who have worked at least 200 days per year. For employees who have worked less than 200 days, the number of days of leave will be calculated proportionally. To obtain more accurate information about your personal entitlement, additional details are needed, such as length of service and the scope of the position.

According to the Hours of Work and Rest Law, 5711-1951, a work week may not exceed forty-five hours of work. The law also stipulates that between one workday and the next there shall be a break of at least eight hours. Therefore, according to the law, it is possible to work up to 6 days a week, as long as the 45-hour weekly limit is not exceeded and a break of at least 8 hours is maintained between workdays.

According to the law, a single parent is entitled to be absent from work to care for their child due to the closure of the educational institution due to a state of emergency, even if they do not have accrued vacation days. The law states that an employer will not fire an employee for such absence, when the child is in the sole custody of the employee or the employee is the child's single parent. The absence is permitted for up to 16 days per year. It is important to note that this absence is not at the expense of the employee's vacation days, but is protected by law as an excused absence due to the state of emergency.
The law does not specifically address the situation where more than 16 days per year are needed. However, the law defines the maximum allowable absence due to the illness of a child. Under the law, an employee who is a single parent or has sole custody of the child is entitled to up to 16 days per year. In other cases, the entitlement is up to 8 days per year. If more days are needed, it may be necessary to use vacation days or discuss this with the employer.
According to the law, a soldier serving in permanent service is considered a dismissed employee for the purpose of determining his rights in connection with dismissals in two cases: 1. If the permanent service was not preceded by a period of uninterrupted compulsory service, and the soldier was a permanent employee in the factory before the start of permanent service - from the date of the start of permanent service. 2. If the permanent service was preceded by a period of uninterrupted compulsory service, and the soldier was a permanent employee in the factory immediately before his enlistment in compulsory service - from the date on which he began serving permanent service under an obligation for a period that, together with all previous uninterrupted permanent service periods, exceeds two years. Beyond that, the law does not specify specific employment conditions for permanent soldiers.

According to the law, if you worked in parallel with reserve service during hours other than your regular working hours, you are entitled to receive both your regular salary and reserve compensation. That is, you are entitled to reimbursement for the reserve days in addition to your regular salary. According to the Annual Leave Law, the number of days of annual leave depends on your seniority with the employer: - In the first five years: 16 days of leave per year - In the sixth year: 18 days of leave - In the seventh year: 21 days of leave - From the eighth year onwards: an additional day for each year of work, up to a maximum of 28 days of leave per year It is important to note that this entitlement is for employees who have worked at least 200 days per year. If you have worked less than 200 days, the number of days of leave will be calculated proportionally. Also, if you have worked only part of the year, the entitlement will be calculated according to the number of days actually worked, with 240 days of work or more entitling you to the full number of days of leave for that year.
No, the employer cannot delete vacation days for someone who was in the reserves. According to the Annual Vacation Law, Section 5(a)(1), the days the employee served in the reserves will not be included in the number of vacation days. In other words, the reserve days are not considered vacation days and cannot be deleted from the employee's vacation days. Furthermore, if reserve days occurred within a planned vacation period, the vacation should be considered as terminated for those days and should be completed as much as possible in the same work year.

According to the Discharged Soldiers (Return to Work) Law, 1949, after being discharged from regular service and then reserve service, you have a number of rights: 1. Seniority rights: The period between your enlistment and your acceptance into employment is considered a period of work in the factory for the purpose of calculating seniority at work. This includes rights that depend on seniority at work, whether by virtue of the law, custom, or an employment contract. 2. Continuity of service: If you returned and enlisted within three months of your discharge, your first period of service is considered to have continued without interruption until the end of your second period of service. 3. Rights as a foreign conscript: If you served as a foreign conscript, you are subject to the same laws as a soldier regarding return to work, prohibition of dismissal, and continuity of work. It is important to note that these rights depend on the specific circumstances of your case and the working conditions at your place of work. It is recommended that you check your specific rights with your employer or an authorized entity.

By law, you must notify your employer of your call-up for reserve service within a reasonable time after you begin work at the factory. In your case, since you started work only one day before your call-up for reserve service, you must notify your employer as soon as possible. It is important to note that if there are no restrictions on the part of the military or the employer, you can perform work concurrently with reserve service. Under Israeli law, employees cannot automatically request remote work. The decision to allow remote work is part of the employer’s administrative prerogative. However, the employer must consider the employee’s request to work from home in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the prevailing circumstances. In other words, while employees can request to work remotely, the final decision rests with the employer.
 According to the law, the decision to work remotely is part of the employer's administrative right. However, the employer must consider the employee's request to work remotely in good faith and in a matter-of-fact manner given the existing circumstances. According to the law, the employer cannot unilaterally place an employee on unpaid leave (GLAT). Taking unpaid leave requires mutual consent of the employer and employee. If the employer requests to take you on unpaid leave, you have the right to refuse. However, there are special cases in which the law allows taking unpaid leave under certain conditions, such as in the case of a pregnant employee (after receiving a special permit) or spouses of reserve service members. If you are in such a special situation, it is recommended to check your specific rights. If the employer insists on taking you on unpaid leave without your consent, this may be considered a violation of your rights as an employee. In such a case, it is recommended to consult a professional in the field of labor law.
According to the law, the payment you receive through your employer will be reflected in your salary. The Sick Pay Law states that "sick pay paid by an employer is treated as wages for all purposes." In other words, if you are entitled to sick pay, it will be paid to you as part of your regular salary. Regarding other entitlements or additional payments, this depends on your specific situation and the employer's decisions. For example, if the employer received compensation for paying wages to employees who were evacuated from their homes during the war, you may be entitled to wages even if you did not come to work. It is important to note that in some cases, such as reserve service, the compensation is provided by the National Insurance Institute, but is sometimes transferred through the employer. If you have additional questions or a specific case, it is recommended to contact your employer or the relevant authorities for more accurate information.

 According to the law, entitlement to compensation does not depend on the number of jobs you have changed, but on the specific circumstances of the termination of employment at each place. The law states that the employee's rights to compensation are preserved even if he has moved between several jobs, as long as the conditions that entitle him to compensation at each separate place of work are met. However, because the question is general and there is no specific information regarding the circumstances of the termination of employment at each place, it is not possible to determine definitively whether you are entitled to compensation. It is recommended to examine the specific circumstances of the termination of employment at each separate place of work to determine your entitlement to compensation.

 According to the Emergency Labor Service Law, 5727-1967, Section 21, a conscript may not be dismissed from his job for which he was drafted, except with written permission from the General Inspector of Manpower. This law applies to workers drafted under Order 8, without distinction between salaried and self-employed workers. Therefore, it is prohibited to dismiss a self-employed worker drafted under Order 8 without the aforementioned permission.

No, it is prohibited to fire employees who have received Order 8 (Reserve Recruitment Order) without special permission. According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee due to his service in the reserves, his call to reserve service, or his expected service in the reserves. If the employee serves in the reserves for more than two consecutive days, he may not be fired for 30 days after the end of reserve service without permission from the Employment Committee. If reserve service lasts more than 60 days, the period of protection from dismissal is extended to 60 days after the end of service. Dismissals in violation of these provisions will be void.

No, you may not be fired during maternity leave. According to the Women's Labor Law, an employer may not fire a female employee during the period of childbirth and parenthood (maternity leave). In addition, the law prohibits firing for 60 days after the end of the period of childbirth and parenthood, unless a special permit has been received from the Ministry of Labor. Firings in violation of these provisions are void under the law.

No, it is not illegal to terminate an employee’s employment because of their request for Sunday as a day of rest. According to Section 9C(a) of the Hours of Work and Rest Act, an employer may not refuse to hire an individual solely because they have indicated that they do not agree to work on the weekly rest day as prohibited by their religious precepts. The law protects the right of employees of all religions, including Christian employees, to observe their religious day of rest. Therefore, terminating an employee’s employment under these circumstances constitutes a violation of the law.

Yes, a Christian worker is permitted to request Sunday as a weekly day of rest. According to the Hours of Work and Rest Law, 5711-1951, Section 7(b)(2), for a non-Jew, the weekly rest can include the Sabbath or the first or sixth day of the week, all according to what is acceptable to him as his weekly day of rest. Therefore, a Christian worker is permitted to request that Sunday be his weekly day of rest, according to what is acceptable to him.

 According to the information provided, employees who were absent from work between 07.10.2023 and 30.6.2024 due to the security situation and who meet certain criteria are entitled to reimbursement of vacation days they took due to the situation. The criteria include, among others, employees living in an evacuated settlement, employees in educational institutions that were closed, and parents who were absent to care for their children due to the closure of educational institutions. The employer is required to pay wages to these employees and may be entitled to a refund from the Tax Authority. It is important to note that there are specific conditions for each case, and it is recommended to check the exact eligibility with the employer or the relevant authorities.
 According to the law, an employer is not permitted to fire an employee for being absent from work to care for their child due to the closure of the educational institution where the child is studying or staying during a special situation in the home front. This is provided that the child is in the sole custody of the employee or that the employee is an independent parent, or that the employee's spouse is not absent from work for this purpose. However, the law does not specifically address the payment of wages for these days of absence. Therefore, it is recommended to check the employment agreement or contact the employer to clarify your rights in this regard.
According to the Discharged Soldiers (Return to Work) Law, 1949, Section 12: A discharged soldier who returns to work in a factory where employees are granted rights dependent on seniority in work (whether by virtue of law, custom, or an employment contract), the period between his enlistment and his return to work will be considered a period of work in the factory for the purpose of calculating seniority. That is, the period of military service is considered a period of work for the purpose of calculating seniority in salary for discharged soldiers who have returned to their jobs.

According to Israeli law, an employer may not refuse to hire a person solely because he has announced that he does not agree to work on the weekly rest days according to a prohibition in his religious commandments. Section 9C(a) of the Working Hours and Rest Law explicitly states that "a person in need of an employee shall not refuse to hire a person solely because he announced upon hiring that he does not agree to work on the weekly rest days according to a prohibition in his religious commandments which he observes." In the event of a job offer being canceled because of a Christian employee's request to accept Sunday as his day of rest, the employee may apply to the appropriate legal authorities and claim prohibited discrimination on religious grounds. The law protects the employee's right to observe his religious day of rest, and prohibits the employer from discriminating against him for this reason.

According to the law, there are several situations in which it is prohibited to fire employees without special permission. For example, it is prohibited to fire a pregnant employee, an employee on maternity leave or during a certain period after it, an employee undergoing fertility treatments, an employee in the reserves and during a certain period after the reserves, and employees on paid sick leave. Also, during a state of emergency or war, there are additional restrictions on firing. To know whether you are specifically allowed to be fired, additional information is needed regarding your personal situation and the specific circumstances. If you think that the firing is illegal, it is recommended to consult a professional or contact the Ministry of Labor.
According to the law, there are several situations in which it is prohibited to fire employees without special permission. For example, it is prohibited to fire a pregnant employee, an employee on maternity leave or during a certain period after it, an employee undergoing fertility treatments, an employee in the reserves and during a certain period after the reserves, and employees who were absent from work due to the security emergency. There are also special protections for employees who themselves or their family members have been injured or evacuated due to the security emergency. Without additional information about your specific circumstances, it is not possible to determine with certainty whether you are allowed or prohibited from being fired. It is recommended to consult a professional regarding your individual case.
According to the Women's Labor Law, an employer is prohibited from dismissing a female employee during the period of childbirth and parenthood (maternity leave). Dismissals during maternity leave are against the law and void. The law also prohibits giving notice of dismissal for a date beginning during the period of childbirth and parenthood. If you were dismissed during maternity leave, the dismissal is illegal and you are entitled to return to your job.
According to the law, if you have received Order 8 (a reserve order in emergency circumstances), you are not automatically entitled to receive full pay from your employer during your reserve service. However, you are entitled to reserve service compensation from the National Insurance Institute. It is important to note that if you work concurrently with your reserve service (during hours other than service hours), you are entitled to receive pay for the work you performed in addition to the reserve compensation. For further details regarding the compensation and rights you are entitled to, it is recommended to contact the National Insurance Institute.

According to the law, it is prohibited to fire an employee for his service in the reserves or during the period of reserve service. Protection against dismissal depends on the duration of reserve service: - If the reserve service is more than two consecutive days and less than 60 days, the employee may not be fired during the service and 30 days after its completion without special permission. - If the reserve service is more than 60 days, the employee may not be fired during the service and 60 days after its completion without special permission. It is important to note that your wife's employment status does not affect your protection against dismissal during and after reserve service.
According to Israeli law, eligibility for maternity benefits from the National Insurance Institute does not depend on the specific workplace, but on the qualifying period you have accumulated. If you have worked and accumulated a sufficient qualifying period (10 months out of 14 or 15 months out of 22 months preceding the birth), you will be eligible for maternity benefits even if you switch to freelance work. However, it is important to note that as a freelancer, you must take care of your National Insurance payments yourself in order to maintain your rights. It is recommended that you check your eligibility status with the National Insurance Institute before switching to self-employment, to ensure that you do not lose rights.

For reserve service over 60 days: It is prohibited to fire during the service and 60 days after its completion without a permit. 2. For reserve service over two consecutive days and up to 60 days: It is prohibited to fire during the service and 30 days after its completion without a permit. According to the Sick Pay Law, 1976, an employee is entitled to accrue one and a half days of sick leave for each full month of work. That is, in a full work year (12 months), an employee is entitled to 18 sick days (12 * 1.5 = 18). It is important to note that this is the annual entitlement to accrue sick days, and not necessarily the number of days the employee can use in a particular year. The maximum entitlement to sick pay is limited to 90 days in total, minus the periods during which the employee has already received sick pay.

Yes, you have rights at your workplace when your spouse is drafted under Order 8. According to the Women's Employment Law, you are entitled to be absent from work for one hour a day, starting from the first day of your spouse's reserve service, under the following conditions: 1. Your spouse's reserve period will not be less than five consecutive days. 2. You have a child under the age of 13 who is with you. 3. You are employed full-time according to the custom at your workplace. 4. You have notified your employer of the exercise of the right and presented confirmation of your spouse's reserve service. In addition, according to the Discharged Soldiers Law, you have protection against dismissal or being taken on unpaid leave during your spouse's reserve service period and for 14 days after the end of the service, provided that the reserve service is in emergency circumstances or lasted at least 21 consecutive days. It is important to note that absence from work during this period will not affect the continuity of your employment or the rights dependent on seniority.
Yes, you have rights at your workplace when your spouse is drafted under Order 8. By law, you are entitled to protection from dismissal or unpaid leave during your spouse's reserve service period and for 14 days after the end of the service, provided that the reserve service is at least 21 consecutive days or in emergency circumstances. In addition, if you have a child under the age of 13, you are entitled to be absent from work for one hour a day starting from the first day of your spouse's reserve service, provided that the reserve period is at least 5 consecutive days and you are employed full-time. You must notify your employer of the exercise of this right and present confirmation of your spouse's reserve service. It is important to note that absence from work during this period will not be considered a break in the continuity of your work and will not affect your rights dependent on your seniority with the employer.
